</td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><div class="ib-country-website"><b>Website</b><br/><a class="external text" href="https://www.un.org/en/" rel="nofollow">un.org</a> (General)<br/><a class="external text" href="https://www.un.int" rel="nofollow">un.int</a> (Permanent Missions)</div></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2">

<td style="text-align:center; border:0; padding-bottom:0"><div id="before-after"></div> <b>Preceded by</b></td>
<td style="text-align:center;border:0; padding-bottom:0;">
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:top; text-align:center; border:0;">
<table style="width:100%; background: transparent; text-align:center; margin:0 auto; border:0;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle;"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Flag_of_the_League_of_Nations_%281939%29.svg/20px-Flag_of_the_League_of_Nations_%281939%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Flag_of_the_League_of_Nations_%281939%29.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_League_of_Nations_%281939%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Flag_of_the_League_of_Nations_%281939%29.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_League_of_Nations_%281939%29.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
</td>
<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle; text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>
</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top; text-align:center;border:0;">
</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>United Nations</b> (<b>UN</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental organization</a> whose stated purposes are to maintain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_peace" title="International peace">international peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_security" title="International security">security</a>, develop friendly relations among nations, achieve international cooperation, and be a centre for harmonizing the actions of nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> It is the world's largest and most familiar international organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The UN is <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">headquartered</a> on <a href="/wiki/Extraterritoriality" title="Extraterritoriality">international territory</a> in New York City, and has other main offices in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Geneva" title="United Nations Office at Geneva">Geneva</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Nairobi" title="United Nations Office at Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Vienna" title="United Nations Office at Vienna">Vienna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peace_Palace" title="Peace Palace">The Hague</a> (home to the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>).
</p><p>The UN was established after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> <a href="/wiki/Dumbarton_Oaks_Conference" title="Dumbarton Oaks Conference">with the aim of preventing future wars</a>, succeeding the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, which was characterized as ineffective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> On 25 April 1945, 50 governments met in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> for <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization" title="United Nations Conference on International Organization">a conference</a> and started drafting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" title="United Nations Charter">UN Charter</a>, which was adopted on 25 June 1945 and took effect on 24 October 1945, when the UN began operations. Pursuant to the Charter, the organization's objectives include maintaining international peace and security, protecting <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>, delivering <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian aid</a>, promoting <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>, and upholding <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> At its founding, the UN had 51 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member states</a>; with the addition of <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> in 2011, membership is now 193, representing almost all of the world's <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_SouthSudan_193rd_state_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_SouthSudan_193rd_state-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>The organization's mission to preserve world peace was complicated in its early decades by the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> between the United States and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and their respective allies. Its missions have consisted primarily of unarmed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Military_Observer" title="United Nations Military Observer">military observers</a> and lightly armed troops with primarily monitoring, reporting and confidence-building roles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> UN membership grew significantly following widespread <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> beginning in the 1960s. Since then, 80 former colonies have gained independence, including 11 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trust_territories" title="Trust territories">trust territories</a> that had been monitored by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">Trusteeship Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> By the 1970s, the UN's budget for economic and social development programmes far outstripped its spending on <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a>. After the end of the Cold War, the UN shifted and expanded its field operations, undertaking a wide variety of complex tasks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>The UN has six principal organs: the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly</a>; the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>; the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">Economic and Social Council</a> (ECOSOC); the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">Trusteeship Council</a>; the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>; and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Secretariat" title="UN Secretariat">UN Secretariat</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_System" title="UN System">UN System</a> includes a multitude of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specialized_agencies" title="Specialized agencies">specialized agencies</a>, funds and programmes such as the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, and <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organizations</a> may be granted consultative status with ECOSOC and other agencies to participate in the UN's work.
</p><p>The UN's chief administrative officer is the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">secretary-general</a>, currently Portuguese politician and diplomat <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a>, who began his first five year-term on 1 January 2017 and was re-elected on 8 June 2021. The organization is financed by assessed and voluntary contributions from its member states.
</p><p>The UN, its officers, and its agencies have won many <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prizes</a>, though other evaluations of its effectiveness have been mixed. Some commentators believe the organization to be an important force for peace and human development, while others have called it ineffective, biased, or corrupt.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_Nations" title="History of the United Nations">History of the United Nations</a></div>
<h3><span id="Background_.28pre-1941.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_(pre-1941)">Background (pre-1941)</span></h3>
<p>In the century prior to the UN's creation, several <a href="/wiki/International_organization" title="International organization">international organizations</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a> were formed to ensure protection and assistance for victims of armed conflict and strife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>During World War I, several major leaders, especially US President <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Woodrow_Wilson_administration" title="Foreign policy of the Woodrow Wilson administration">Woodrow Wilson</a>, advocated for a world body to guarantee peace. The winners of the war, the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a>, met to hammer out formal peace terms at the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference_(1919%E2%80%931920)" title="Paris Peace Conference (1919–1920)">Paris Peace Conference</a>. The <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> was approved, and started operations, but the U.S. never joined. On 10 January 1920, the League of Nations formally came into being when the Covenant of the League of Nations, ratified by 42 nations in 1919, took effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The League Council acted as a type of executive body directing the Assembly's business. It began with four permanent members – <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">the United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>. 
</p><p>After some limited successes and failures during the 1920s, the League proved ineffective in the 1930s. It failed to act against the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">Japanese invasion of Manchuria</a> in 1933. Forty nations voted for Japan to withdraw from <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> but Japan voted against it and walked out of the League instead of withdrawing from Manchuria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> It also failed against the <a href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="Second Italo-Ethiopian War">Second Italo-Ethiopian War</a> when calls for economic sanctions against Italy failed. Italy and other nations left the league. All of them realized that it had failed and they began to re-arm as fast as possible.
</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_II" title="Causes of World War II">war broke out in 1939</a>, the League closed down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Declarations_by_the_Allies_of_World_War_II_.281941.E2.80.931944.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Declarations_by_the_Allies_of_World_War_II_(1941–1944)">Declarations by the Allies of World War II (1941–1944)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1659" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg/220px-United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg/330px-United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg/440px-United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_organization_sketch_by_Franklin_Roosevelt_with_the_Four_Policemen_in_1943.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1943 sketch by Franklin Roosevelt of the UN original three branches: The <a href="/wiki/Four_Policemen" title="Four Policemen">Four Policemen</a>, an executive branch, and an international assembly of forty UN member states</div></div></div>
<p>The first specific step towards the establishment of the United Nations was the Inter-Allied conference that led to the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_St_James%27s_Palace" title="Declaration of St James's Palace">Declaration of St James's Palace</a> on 12 June 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> By August 1941, American president <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin Roosevelt</a> and British prime minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> had drafted the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Charter" title="Atlantic Charter">Atlantic Charter</a> to define goals for the post-war world. At the subsequent meeting of the Inter-Allied Council in London on 24 September 1941, the eight <a href="/wiki/List_of_governments_in_exile_during_World_War_II" title="List of governments in exile during World War II">governments in exile of countries under Axis occupation</a>, together with the Soviet Union and representatives of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_French_Forces" title="Free French Forces">Free French Forces</a>, unanimously adopted adherence to the common principles of policy set forth by Britain and United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>President Roosevelt and Prime Minister Churchill met at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> in December 1941 for the <a href="/wiki/Arcadia_Conference" title="Arcadia Conference">Arcadia Conference</a>. Roosevelt, considered a founder of the UN,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> coined the term <i>United Nations</i> to describe the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied countries</a>. Churchill accepted it, noting its use by <a href="/wiki/Lord_Byron" title="Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The text of the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">Declaration by United Nations</a> was drafted on 29 December 1941, by Roosevelt, Churchill, and Roosevelt aide <a href="/wiki/Harry_Hopkins" title="Harry Hopkins">Harry Hopkins</a>. It incorporated Soviet suggestions but included no role for France. One major change from the Atlantic Charter was the addition of a provision for religious freedom, which Stalin approved after Roosevelt insisted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESherwood1948447–453_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESherwood1948447–453-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt's idea of the "<a href="/wiki/Four_Policemen" title="Four Policemen">Four Powers</a>", referring to the four major Allied countries, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">Republic of China</a>, emerged in the Declaration by United Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sheriff_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-sheriff-24">[24]</a></sup> On New Year's Day 1942, President Roosevelt, Prime Minister Churchill, <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Litvinov" title="Maxim Litvinov">Maxim Litvinov</a>, of the USSR, and <a href="/wiki/T._V._Soong" title="T. V. Soong">T. V. Soong</a>, of China, signed the "<a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">Declaration by United Nations</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> and the next day the representatives of twenty-two other nations added their signatures. During the war, "the United Nations" became the official term for the Allies. To join, countries had to sign the Declaration and declare war on the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2003_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2003-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>The October 1943 <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Conference_(1943)" title="Moscow Conference (1943)">Moscow Conference</a> resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Declarations" title="Moscow Declarations">Moscow Declarations</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_the_Four_Nations" title="Declaration of the Four Nations">Four Power Declaration on General Security</a> which aimed for the creation "at the earliest possible date of a general international organization". This was the first public announcement that a new international organization was being contemplated to replace the League of Nations. The <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran Conference</a> followed shortly afterwards at which Roosevelt, Churchill and Stalin met and discussed the idea of a post-war international organization.
</p><p>The new international organization was formulated and negotiated among the delegations from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Four_(World_War_II)" title="Big Four (World War II)">Allied Big Four</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Dumbarton_Oaks_Conference" title="Dumbarton Oaks Conference">Dumbarton Oaks Conference</a> from 21 September to 7 October 1944. They agreed on proposals for the aims, structure and functioning of the new international organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> It took the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">conference at Yalta</a> in February 1945, and further negotiations with Moscow, before all the issues were resolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Founding_.281945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_(1945)">Founding (1945)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1450" decoding="async" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png/440px-United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png/660px-United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png/880px-United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png 2x" width="440"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Member_States-1945.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The UN in 1945: founding members in light blue, protectorates and territories of the founding members in dark blue</div></div></div>
<p>By 1 March 1945, 21 additional states had signed the Declaration by United Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOsmańczyk20042445_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOsmańczyk20042445-31">[31]</a></sup> After months of planning, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization" title="United Nations Conference on International Organization">UN Conference on International Organization</a> opened in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, 25 April 1945, attended by 50 governments and a number of non-governmental organizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charter_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Charter-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNHistory_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNHistory-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The Big Four sponsoring countries invited other nations to take part and the heads of the delegations of the four chaired the plenary meetings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Winston Churchill urged Roosevelt to restore France to its status of a major Power after the liberation of Paris in August 1944. The drafting of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a> was completed over the following two months; it was signed on 26 June 1945 by the representatives of the 50 countries. <a href="/wiki/Jan_Smuts" title="Jan Smuts">Jan Smuts</a> was a principal author of the draft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The UN officially came into existence on 24 October 1945, upon ratification of the Charter by the five permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>—the US, the UK, France, the Soviet Union and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">the Republic of China</a>—and by a majority of the other 46 signatories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmilestones1941to1950_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first meetings of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Assembly" title="General Assembly">General Assembly</a>, with 51 nations represented,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[a]</a></sup> and the Security Council took place in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> beginning in January 1946.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmilestones1941to1950_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-38">[38]</a></sup> Debates began at once, covering topical issues such as the presence of Russian troops in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_Azerbaijan" title="Iranian Azerbaijan">Iranian Azerbaijan</a>, British forces in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and within days the first <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">veto</a> was cast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> British diplomat <a href="/wiki/Gladwyn_Jebb" title="Gladwyn Jebb">Gladwyn Jebb</a> served as acting secretary-general.
</p><p>The General Assembly selected <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> as the site for the headquarters of the UN, construction began on 14 September 1948 and the facility was completed on 9 October 1952. Its site—like UN headquarters buildings in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>—is designated as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_territory" title="International territory">international territory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009149–151_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009149–151-43">[42]</a></sup> The Norwegian foreign minister, <a href="/wiki/Trygve_Lie" title="Trygve Lie">Trygve Lie</a>, was elected as the first <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN secretary-general</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmilestones1941to1950_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Cold_War_.281947.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_(1947–1991)">Cold War (1947–1991)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3462" data-file-width="2442" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld.jpg/170px-Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld.jpg/255px-Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld.jpg/340px-Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld" title="Dag Hammarskjöld">Dag Hammarskjöld</a> was a particularly active secretary-general from 1953 until his death in 1961.</div></div></div>
<p>Though the UN's primary mandate was <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a>, the division between the US and USSR often paralysed the organization, generally allowing it to intervene only in conflicts distant from the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199535_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199535-44">[43]</a></sup> Two notable exceptions were a Security Council resolution on 7 July 1950 authorizing a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Command" title="United Nations Command">US-led coalition</a> to repel the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">North Korean invasion of South Korea</a>, passed in the absence of the USSR,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmilestones1941to1950_38-3"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199558–59_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199558–59-45">[44]</a></sup> and the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Armistice_Agreement" title="Korean Armistice Agreement">Korean Armistice Agreement</a> on 27 July 1953.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 November 1947, the General Assembly approved <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">a resolution</a> to partition <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a>, approving the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">state of Israel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Two years later, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bunche" title="Ralph Bunche">Ralph Bunche</a>, a UN official, negotiated an armistice to the resulting conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199551–54_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199551–54-48">[47]</a></sup> On 7 November 1956, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Emergency_Force" title="United Nations Emergency Force">first UN peacekeeping force</a> was established to end the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmilestones1951to1960_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1951to1960-49">[48]</a></sup> however, the UN was unable to intervene against the USSR's simultaneous invasion of Hungary following <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">that country's revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995114_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995114-50">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 July 1960, the UN established <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Operation_in_the_Congo" title="United Nations Operation in the Congo">United Nations Operation in the Congo</a> (UNOC), the largest military force of its early decades, to bring order to the breakaway <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">State of Katanga</a>, restoring it to the control of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> by 11 May 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995115–134_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995115–134-51">[50]</a></sup> While traveling to meet rebel leader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moise_Tshombe" title="Moise Tshombe">Moise Tshombe</a> during the conflict, <a href="/wiki/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld" title="Dag Hammarskjöld">Dag Hammarskjöld</a>, often named as one of the UN's most effective secretaries-general,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1961_Ndola_United_Nations_DC-6_crash" title="1961 Ndola United Nations DC-6 crash">died in a plane crash</a>; months later he was posthumously awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995127–128,_134_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995127–128,_134-53">[52]</a></sup> In 1964, Hammarskjöld's successor, <a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a>, deployed the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Peacekeeping_Force_in_Cyprus" title="United Nations Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus">UN Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus</a>, which would become one of the UN's longest-running peacekeeping missions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995156–157_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995156–157-54">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>With the spread of <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> in the 1960s, the organization's membership saw an influx of newly independent nations. In 1960 alone, 17 new states joined the UN, 16 of them from Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmilestones1951to1960_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1951to1960-49">[48]</a></sup> On 25 October 1971, with opposition from the United States, but with the support of many <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a> nations, the mainland, communist <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> was given the Chinese seat on the Security Council in place of the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a>; the vote was widely seen as a sign of waning US influence in the organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995195–197_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995195–197-55">[54]</a></sup> Third World nations organized into the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a> coalition under the leadership of Algeria, which briefly became a dominant power at the UN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995208–210_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995208–210-56">[55]</a></sup> On 10 November 1975, a bloc comprising the USSR and Third World nations passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_3379" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 3379">a resolution</a>, over the strenuous US and Israeli opposition, declaring <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">Zionism</a> to be racism; the resolution was repealed on 16 December 1991, shortly after the end of the Cold War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995204–226,_213,_220–221_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995204–226,_213,_220–221-57">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>With an increasing Third World presence and the failure of UN mediation in conflicts in the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1965" title="Indo-Pakistani War of 1965">Kashmir</a>, the UN increasingly shifted its attention to its ostensibly secondary goals of economic development and cultural exchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995167–168,_224–225_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995167–168,_224–225-59">[58]</a></sup> By the 1970s, the UN budget for social and economic development was far greater than its peacekeeping budget.
</p>
<h3><span id="Post.E2.80.93Cold_War_.281991.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post–Cold_War_(1991–present)">Post–Cold War (1991–present)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kofi_Annan_2012_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2828" data-file-width="2255" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Kofi_Annan_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kofi_Annan_2012_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, secretary-general from 1997 to 2006</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UN_Members_Flags2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="1840" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/UN_Members_Flags2.JPG/220px-UN_Members_Flags2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/UN_Members_Flags2.JPG/330px-UN_Members_Flags2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/UN_Members_Flags2.JPG/440px-UN_Members_Flags2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UN_Members_Flags2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flags of member nations at the <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">United Nations Headquarters</a>, seen in 2007</div></div></div>
<p>After the Cold War, the UN saw a radical expansion in its peacekeeping duties, taking on more missions in five years than it had in the previous four decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Between 1988 and 2000, the number of adopted Security Council resolutions more than doubled, and the peacekeeping budget increased more than tenfold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> The UN negotiated an end to the <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">Salvadoran Civil War</a>, launched a successful <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transition_Assistance_Group" title="United Nations Transition Assistance Group">peacekeeping mission in Namibia</a>, and oversaw democratic elections in post-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apartheid_in_South_Africa" title="Apartheid in South Africa">apartheid</a> South Africa and post-<a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> Cambodia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> In 1991, the UN authorized a <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">US-led coalition</a> that repulsed the Iraqi <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" title="Invasion of Kuwait">invasion of Kuwait</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995264–277_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995264–277-65">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Urquhart" title="Brian Urquhart">Brian Urquhart</a>, under-secretary-general from 1971 to 1985, later described the hopes raised by these successes as a "false renaissance" for the organization, given the more troubled missions that followed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995334_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995334-66">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in the last decades of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, American and European critics of the UN condemned the organization for perceived mismanagement and corruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995226–227_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995226–227-67">[66]</a></sup> In 1984, US President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>, withdrew his nation's funding from <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization</a> (UNESCO) over allegations of mismanagement, followed by the UK and Singapore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995234–237_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995234–237-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boutros_Boutros-Ghali" title="Boutros Boutros-Ghali">Boutros Boutros-Ghali</a>, secretary-general from 1992 to 1996, initiated a reform of the Secretariat, reducing the size of the organization somewhat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995285–286_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995285–286-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NST_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-NST-71">[70]</a></sup> His successor, <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> (1997–2006), initiated further management reforms in the face of threats from the US to withhold its UN dues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NST_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-NST-71">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p>Though the UN Charter had been written primarily to prevent aggression by one nation against another, in the early 1990s the UN faced a number of simultaneous, serious crises within nations such as Somalia, Haiti, Mozambique, and the former Yugoslavia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy200766–67_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy200766–67-72">[71]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Operation_in_Somalia_II" title="United Nations Operation in Somalia II">UN mission in Somalia</a> was widely viewed as a failure after the US withdrawal following casualties in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mogadishu_(1993)" title="Battle of Mogadishu (1993)">Battle of Mogadishu</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Protection_Force" title="United Nations Protection Force">UN mission to Bosnia</a> faced "worldwide ridicule" for its indecisive and confused mission in the face of ethnic cleansing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> In 1994, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Assistance_Mission_for_Rwanda" title="United Nations Assistance Mission for Rwanda">UN Assistance Mission for Rwanda</a> failed to intervene in the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a> amid indecision in the Security Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007104_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007104-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the late 1990s to the early 2000s, international interventions authorized by the UN took a wider variety of forms. <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1244" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1244">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1244</a> authorised the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">Kosovo Force</a> beginning in 1999. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Sierra_Leone" title="United Nations Mission in Sierra Leone">UN mission (1999-2006)</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">Sierra Leone Civil War</a> was supplemented by a <a href="/wiki/British_military_intervention_in_the_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="British military intervention in the Sierra Leone Civil War">British military intervention</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">invasion of Afghanistan in 2001</a> was overseen by NATO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007110–111_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007110–111-75">[74]</a></sup> In 2003, the United States <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invaded Iraq</a> despite failing to pass a UN Security Council resolution for authorization, prompting a new round of questioning of the organization's effectiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007111_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007111-76">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>Under the eighth secretary-general, <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>, the UN intervened with peacekeepers in crises such as the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Darfur" title="War in Darfur">War in Darfur</a> in Sudan and the <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">Kivu conflict</a> in the Democratic Republic of Congo and sent observers and chemical weapons inspectors to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General%27s_Internal_Review_Panel_on_United_Nations_Action_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Secretary-General's Internal Review Panel on United Nations Action in Sri Lanka">an internal review</a> of UN actions in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alleged_war_crimes_during_the_final_stages_of_the_Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Alleged war crimes during the final stages of the Sri Lankan Civil War">the final battles</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Sri Lankan Civil War">Sri Lankan Civil War</a> in 2009 concluded that the organization had suffered "systemic failure".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> In 2010, the organization suffered the worst loss of life in its history, when 101 personnel died in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">Haiti earthquake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmilestones2001to2010_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones2001to2010-79">[78]</a></sup> Acting under <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1973" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973</a> in 2011, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> countries intervened in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libyan_Civil_War_(2011)" title="Libyan Civil War (2011)">Libyan Civil War</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Summit" title="Millennium Summit">Millennium Summit</a> was held in 2000 to discuss the UN's role in the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCagenda_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCagenda-80">[79]</a></sup> The three-day meeting was the largest gathering of world leaders in history, and culminated in the adoption by all member states of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a> (MDGs), a commitment to achieve international development in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">poverty reduction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a>. Progress towards these goals, which were to be met by 2015, was ultimately uneven. The <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Summit" title="2005 World Summit">2005 World Summit</a> reaffirmed the UN's focus on promoting development, peacekeeping, human rights, and global security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> were launched in 2015 to succeed the Millennium Development Goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sustainable_Development_Goals_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Development_Goals-82">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to addressing global challenges, the UN has sought to improve its accountability and democratic legitimacy by engaging more with civil society and fostering a global constituency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> In an effort to enhance transparency, in 2016 the organization held its first public debate between candidates for secretary-general.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> On 1 January 2017, Portuguese diplomat <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a>, who previously served as <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UN High Commissioner for Refugees</a>, became the ninth secretary-general. Guterres has highlighted several key goals for his administration, including an emphasis on diplomacy for preventing conflicts, more effective peacekeeping efforts, and streamlining the organization to be more responsive and versatile to global needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">United Nations System</a></div>
<p>The United Nations is part of the broader <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">UN system</a>, which includes an extensive network of institutions and entities. Central to the organisation are five principal organs established by the UN Charter: the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly</a> (UNGA), the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> (UNSC), the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">Economic and Social Council</a> (ECOSOC), the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> (ICJ) and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">UN Secretariat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo20043–4_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo20043–4-86">[85]</a></sup> A sixth principal organ, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">Trusteeship Council</a>, suspended operations on 1 November 1994, upon the independence of <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, the last remaining UN trustee territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo20048_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo20048-87">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>Four of the five principal organs are located at the main UN Headquarters in New York City, while the ICJ is seated in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Most other major agencies are based in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Geneva" title="United Nations Office at Geneva">UN offices at Geneva</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Vienna" title="United Nations Office at Vienna">Vienna</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Nairobi" title="United Nations Office at Nairobi">Nairobi</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> additional UN institutions are located throughout the world. The six <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> of the UN, used in intergovernmental meetings and documents, are <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-langs_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-langs-92">[91]</a></sup> On the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Privileges_and_Immunities_of_the_United_Nations" title="Convention on the Privileges and Immunities of the United Nations">Convention on the Privileges and Immunities of the United Nations</a>, the UN and its agencies are <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_immunity" title="Diplomatic immunity">immune</a> from the laws of the countries where they operate, safeguarding the UN's impartiality with regard to host and member countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p>Below the six organs sit, in the words of the author Linda Fasulo, "an amazing collection of entities and organizations, some of which are actually older than the UN itself and operate with almost complete independence from it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo20044_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo20044-94">[93]</a></sup> These include specialized agencies, research and training institutions, programs and funds, and other UN entities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo20044–7_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo20044–7-95">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>All organisations in the UN system obey the <i>Noblemaire principle</i>, which calls for salaries that will attract and retain citizens of countries where compensation is highest, and which ensures equal pay for work of equal value regardless of the employee's nationality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un-salaries_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-un-salaries-96">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> In practice, the <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Service_Commission" title="International Civil Service Commission">International Civil Service Commission</a>, which governs the conditions of UN personnel, takes reference to the highest-paying national civil service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Staff salaries are subject to an internal tax that is administered by the UN organizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un-salaries_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-un-salaries-96">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p><br/>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:-0px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City,_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg" title="Headquarters of the UN in New York City"><img alt="Headquarters of the UN in New York City" data-file-height="1611" data-file-width="3144" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/260px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/390px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/520px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a></div></div></div>
</td>
<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:-32px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_haye_palais_paix_jardin_face.JPG" title="International Court of Justice"><img alt="International Court of Justice" data-file-height="1988" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/La_haye_palais_paix_jardin_face.JPG/260px-La_haye_palais_paix_jardin_face.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/La_haye_palais_paix_jardin_face.JPG/390px-La_haye_palais_paix_jardin_face.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/La_haye_palais_paix_jardin_face.JPG/520px-La_haye_palais_paix_jardin_face.JPG 2x" width="260"/></a></div></div></div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px;padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;font-size:95%;">
<ul><li>May resolve non-compulsory recommendations to states or suggestions to the Security Council (UNSC);</li>
<li>Decides on the admission of new members, following proposal by the UNSC;</li>
<li>Adopts the budget;</li>
<li>Elects the non-permanent members of the UNSC; all members of ECOSOC; the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary-General</a> (following their proposal by the UNSC); and the fifteen judges of the International Court of Justice (ICJ). Each country has one vote.</li></ul>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px;padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;font-size:95%;">
<ul><li>Supports the other <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">UN bodies</a> administratively (for example, in the organization of conferences, the writing of reports and studies and the preparation of the budget);</li>
<li>Its chairperson—the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary-General</a>—is elected by the General Assembly for a five-year mandate and is the UN's foremost representative.</li></ul>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px;padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;font-size:95%;">
<ul><li>Decides disputes between states that recognize its jurisdiction;</li>
<li>Issues legal opinions;</li>
<li>Renders judgment by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relative_majority" title="Relative majority">relative majority</a>. Its fifteen judges are elected by the UN General Assembly for nine-year terms.</li></ul>
</td></tr>

<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:-50px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG" title="UN Economic and Social Council"><img alt="UN Economic and Social Council" data-file-height="1746" data-file-width="3253" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG/260px-United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG/390px-United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG/520px-United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council_chamber_New_York_City_2.JPG 2x" width="260"/></a></div></div></div>
</td>
<td><div style="position:relative;height:120px;overflow:hidden;">
<div style="position:relative;top:0px;left:0px;"><div style="width:100%;overflow-x:hidden;overflow:hidden;">
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG" title="UN Trusteeship Council"><img alt="UN Trusteeship Council" data-file-height="1696" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG/260px-United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG/390px-United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG/520px-United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council_chamber_in_New_York_City_2.JPG 2x" width="260"/></a></div></div></div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px;padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;font-size:95%;">
<ul><li>Responsible for the maintenance of <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">international peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_security" title="International security">security</a>;</li>
<li>May adopt <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_resolution" title="United Nations Security Council resolution">compulsory resolutions</a>;</li>
<li>Has fifteen members: <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">five permanent members</a> with <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">veto power</a> and ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="List of members of the United Nations Security Council">elected members</a>.</li></ul>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px; padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;font-size:95%;">
<ul><li>Responsible for co-operation between states as regards economic and social matters;</li>
<li>Co-ordinates co-operation between the UN's numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">specialized agencies</a>;</li>
<li>Has 54 members, elected by the General Assembly to serve staggered three-year mandates.</li></ul>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;padding-left:15px; padding-bottom:10px;padding-right:10px;font-size:95%;">
<ul><li>Was originally designed to manage colonial possessions that were former <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandates</a>;</li>
<li>Has been inactive since 1994, when <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, the last trust territory, attained independence.</li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_Assembly">General Assembly</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="695" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>, leader of the Soviet Union, addressing the UN General Assembly in December 1988</div></div></div>
<p>The General Assembly is the main <a href="/wiki/Deliberative_assembly" title="Deliberative assembly">deliberative assembly</a> of the UN. Composed of all <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">UN member states</a>, the assembly meets in regular yearly sessions at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Hall" title="United Nations General Assembly Hall">General Assembly Hall</a>, but emergency sessions can also be called.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009131–133_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009131–133-101">[100]</a></sup> The assembly is led by a <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="President of the United Nations General Assembly">president</a>, elected from among the member states on a rotating regional basis, and 21 vice-presidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200469–70_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200469–70-102">[101]</a></sup> The first session convened 10 January 1946 in the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Central_Hall,_Westminster" title="Methodist Central Hall, Westminster">Methodist Central Hall</a> in London and included representatives of 51 nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmilestones1941to1950_38-4"><a href="#cite_note-unmilestones1941to1950-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>When the General Assembly decides on important questions such as those on peace and security, admission of new members and budgetary matters, a two-thirds majority of those present and voting is required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> All other questions are decided by a majority vote. Each member country has one vote. Apart from the approval of budgetary matters, resolutions are not binding on the members. The Assembly may make recommendations on any matters within the scope of the UN, except matters of peace and security that are under consideration by the Security Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009131–133_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009131–133-101">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>Draft resolutions can be forwarded to the General Assembly by its six main committees:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200470–73_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200470–73-105">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Assembly_First_Committee" title="General Assembly First Committee">First Committee (Disarmament and International Security)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Second_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Second Committee">Second Committee (Economic and Financial)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Third_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Third Committee">Third Committee (Social, Humanitarian, and Cultural)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Fourth_Committee" title="United Nations Fourth Committee">Fourth Committee (Special Political and Decolonization)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Fifth_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Fifth Committee">Fifth Committee (Administrative and Budgetary)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Sixth_Committee_(Legal)" title="United Nations General Assembly Sixth Committee (Legal)">Sixth Committee (Legal)</a></li></ul>
<p>As well as by the following two committees:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Committee" title="United Nations General Committee">General Committee</a> – a supervisory committee consisting of the assembly's president, vice-president, and committee heads</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Credentials_Committee" title="United Nations Credentials Committee">Credentials Committee</a> – responsible for determining the credentials of each member nation's UN representatives</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_Council">Security Council</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="835" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg/220px-Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg/330px-Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg/440px-Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colin_Powell_anthrax_vial._5_Feb_2003_at_the_UN.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">Colin Powell</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">US Secretary of State</a>, demonstrates a vial with <a href="/wiki/Legitimacy_of_the_2003_invasion_of_Iraq#Weapons_of_Mass_Destruction" title="Legitimacy of the 2003 invasion of Iraq">alleged</a> <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapon" title="Chemical weapon">chemical weapon</a> probes to the UN Security Council on <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_and_the_Iraq_War" title="United Nations Security Council and the Iraq War">Iraq war</a> hearings, 5 February 2003</div></div></div>
<p>The Security Council is charged with maintaining peace and security among countries. While other organs of the UN can only make "recommendations" to member states, the Security Council has the power to make binding decisions that member states have agreed to carry out, under the terms of Charter Article 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chapter|V_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chapter|V-106">[105]</a></sup> The decisions of the council are known as <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_resolution" title="United Nations Security Council resolution">United Nations Security Council resolutions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200439–43_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200439–43-107">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Security Council is made up of fifteen member states, consisting of five permanent members—China, France, Russia, the United Kingdom, and the United States—and ten non-permanent members elected for two-year terms by the General Assembly: <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> (term ends 2023), <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (2023), <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> (2023), <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> (2023), <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (2022), <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> (2022), <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> (2022), <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (2022), <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (2022), and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> (2023).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> The five permanent members hold <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">veto power</a> over UN resolutions, allowing a permanent member to block adoption of a resolution, though not debate. The ten temporary seats are held for two-year terms, with five member states per year voted in by the General Assembly on a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Regional_Groups" title="United Nations Regional Groups">regional basis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200440–41_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200440–41-109">[108]</a></sup> The presidency of the Security Council rotates alphabetically each month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UN_Secretariat">UN Secretariat</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">United Nations Secretariat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres_2021.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="801" data-file-width="574" decoding="async" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres_2021.jpg/170px-Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres_2021.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres_2021.jpg/255px-Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres_2021.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres_2021.jpg/340px-Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres_2021.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres_2021.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a>, the current <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">secretary-general</a></div></div></div>
<p>The UN Secretariat carries out the day-to-day duties required to operate and maintain the UN system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> It is composed of tens of thousands of international civil servants worldwide and headed by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">secretary-general</a>, who is assisted by the <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Deputy Secretary-General of the United Nations">deputy secretary-general</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200421_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200421-112">[111]</a></sup> The Secretariat's duties include providing information and facilities needed by UN bodies for their meetings; it also carries out tasks as directed by the Security Council, the General Assembly, the Economic and Social Council, and other UN bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009285_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009285-113">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>The secretary-general acts as the <i>de facto</i> spokesperson and leader of the UN. The position is defined in the UN Charter as the organization's "chief administrative officer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> Article 99 of the charter states that the secretary-general can bring to the Security Council's attention "any matter which in his opinion may threaten the maintenance of international peace and security", a phrase that secretaries-general since <a href="/wiki/Trygve_Lie" title="Trygve Lie">Trygve Lie</a> have interpreted as giving the position broad scope for action on the world stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199531–32_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199531–32-115">[114]</a></sup> The office has evolved into a dual role of an administrator of the UN organization and a diplomat and mediator addressing disputes between member states and finding consensus to global issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy200759–62_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy200759–62-116">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>The secretary-general is appointed by the General Assembly, after being recommended by the Security Council, where the permanent members have veto power. There are no specific criteria for the post, but over the years it has become accepted that the position shall be held for one or two terms of five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> The current secretary-general is <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a> of Portugal, who replaced <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> in 2017.
</p>
