<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Court_of_Justice">International Court of Justice</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg/220px-Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg/330px-Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg/440px-Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Hall_de_Justice_de_Palais_de_La_Paix_%C3%A0_La_Haye_Pays-Bas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The ICJ ruled that <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">Kosovo's unilateral declaration of independence</a> from Serbia in 2008 did not violate international law.</div></div></div>
<p>The International Court of Justice (ICJ), sometimes known as the World Court,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica.com_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-119">[118]</a></sup> is the primary judicial organ of the UN. It is the successor to the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_International_Justice" title="Permanent Court of International Justice">Permanent Court of International Justice</a> and occupies that body's former headquarters in the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Palace" title="Peace Palace">Peace Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague, Netherlands</a>, making it the only principal organ not based in New York City. The ICJ's main function is adjudicating disputes among states; it has heard cases concerning war crimes, violations of state sovereignty, ethnic cleansing, and other issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> The court can also be called upon by other UN organs to provide advisory opinions on matters of international law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009183_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009183-121">[120]</a></sup> All UN member states are parties to the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_the_International_Court_of_Justice" title="Statute of the International Court of Justice">ICJ Statute</a>, which forms an integral part of the UN Charter, and nonmembers may also become parties. The ICJ's rulings are binding upon parties and, along with its advisory opinions, serve as <a href="/wiki/Sources_of_international_law" title="Sources of international law">sources of international law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica.com_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-119">[118]</a></sup> The court is composed of 15 judges appointed to nine-year terms by the General Assembly; every sitting judge must be from a different nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009183_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009183-121">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004100–101_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004100–101-122">[121]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_and_Social_Council">Economic and Social Council</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">United Nations Economic and Social Council</a></div>
<p>The Economic and Social Council (ECOSOC) assists the General Assembly in promoting international economic, social, and humanitarian co-operation and development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-123">[122]</a></sup> It was established to serve as the UN's primary forum for global issues and is the largest and most complex UN body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-123">[122]</a></sup> ECOSOC's functions include gathering data, conducting studies, advising member nations, and making recommendations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009103–104_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009103–104-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> Its work is carried out primarily by subsidiary bodies focused on a wide variety of topics; these include the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Permanent_Forum_on_Indigenous_Issues" title="United Nations Permanent Forum on Indigenous Issues">United Nations Permanent Forum on Indigenous Issues</a>, which advises UN agencies on issues relating to <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a>; the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Forum_on_Forests" title="United Nations Forum on Forests">United Nations Forum on Forests</a>, which coordinates and promotes sustainable forest management; the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistical_Commission" title="United Nations Statistical Commission">United Nations Statistical Commission</a>, which co-ordinates information-gathering efforts between agencies; and the <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Sustainable_Development" title="Commission on Sustainable Development">Commission on Sustainable Development</a>, which co-ordinates efforts between UN agencies and NGOs working towards <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>. ECOSOC may also grant consultative status to nongovernmental organizations;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009103–104_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009103–104-124">[123]</a></sup> as of April 2021, close to 5,600 organizations have this status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004156_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004156-126">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specialized_agencies">Specialized agencies</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">List of specialized agencies of the United Nations</a></div>
<p>The UN Charter stipulates that each primary organ of the United Nations can establish various specialized agencies to fulfil its duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CharterIX_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-CharterIX-128">[127]</a></sup> Specialized agencies are autonomous organizations working with the United Nations and each other through the co-ordinating machinery of the Economic and Social Council. Each was integrated into the UN system through an agreement with the UN under UN Charter article 57.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEB_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-CEB-129">[128]</a></sup> There are fifteen specialized agencies, which perform functions as diverse as facilitating international travel, preventing and addressing pandemics, and promoting economic development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[b]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_bodies">Other bodies</span></h3>
<p>The United Nations system includes a myriad of autonomous, separately-administered <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System#Funds_and_programmes,_research_and_training_institutes,_and_other_bodies" title="United Nations System">funds, programmes, research and training institutes, and other subsidiary bodies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-132">[130]</a></sup> Each of these entities have their own area of work, governance structure, and budget; several, such as the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO) and the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> (IAEA), operate independently of the UN but maintain formal partnership agreements. The UN performs much of its humanitarian work through these institutions, such as preventing famine and malnutrition (<a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>), protecting vulnerable and displaced people (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UNHCR</a>), and combating the HIV/AIDS pandemic (<a href="/wiki/Joint_United_Nations_Programme_on_HIV/AIDS" title="Joint United Nations Programme on HIV/AIDS">UNAIDS</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004171–177_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004171–177-133">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">Member states of the United Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_(Member_States_and_Territories).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1399" data-file-width="2756" decoding="async" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg/220px-United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg/330px-United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg/440px-United_Nations_%28Member_States_and_Territories%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_(Member_States_and_Territories).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#009edb; color:black;"> </span> 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">UN Member States</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#9edb00; color:black;"> </span> 2 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">UN Observer States</a> (Palestine, Vatican)</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#db9e00; color:black;"> </span> 2 eligible Non-Member States (Niue, Cook Islands)</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#c0c0c0; color:black;"> </span> 17 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_non-self-governing_territories" title="United Nations list of non-self-governing territories">non-self-governing territories</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#f0f0f0; color:black;"> </span> Antarctica (<a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System" title="Antarctic Treaty System">international territory</a>)</div></div></div></div>
<p>All the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">undisputed</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states" title="List of sovereign states">independent states</a>, apart from <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>, are members of the United Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_SouthSudan_193rd_state_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_SouthSudan_193rd_state-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[c]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, which joined 14 July 2011, is the most recent addition, bringing a total of 193 UN member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-members_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-members-135">[132]</a></sup> The UN Charter outlines the rules for membership:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>1. Membership in the United Nations is open to all other peace-loving states that accept the obligations contained in the present Charter and, in the judgment of the Organization, are able and willing to carry out these obligations.<br/>
</p><p>
2. The admission of any such state to membership in the United Nations will be effected by a decision of the General Assembly upon the recommendation of the Security Council. Chapter II, Article 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[133]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presiden_Sukarno.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4604" data-file-width="3214" decoding="async" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Presiden_Sukarno.jpg/220px-Presiden_Sukarno.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Presiden_Sukarno.jpg/330px-Presiden_Sukarno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Presiden_Sukarno.jpg/440px-Presiden_Sukarno.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Presiden_Sukarno.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Under <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, Indonesia became <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_and_the_United_Nations#Withdrawal_in_1965" title="Indonesia and the United Nations">the first and only country</a> to leave the United Nations.</div></div></div><p>In addition, there are two <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">non-member observer states of the United Nations General Assembly</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> (which holds sovereignty over Vatican City) and the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[134]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">states in free association</a> with <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, are full members of several UN specialized agencies and have had their "full treaty-making capacity" recognized by the Secretariat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art102_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-art102-138">[135]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> is the first and the only nation to withdraw its membership from the United Nations, in protest to the election of Malaysia as a non-permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> in 1965 during <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_confrontation" title="Indonesia–Malaysia confrontation">conflict between the two countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[136]</a></sup> After forming <a href="/wiki/CONEFO" title="CONEFO">CONEFO</a> as a short-lived rival to the UN, Indonesia resumed its full membership in 1966.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_of_77">Group of 77</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a></div>
<p>The Group of 77 (G77) at the UN is a loose coalition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_nations" title="Developing nations">developing nations</a>, designed to promote its members' collective economic interests and create an enhanced joint negotiating capacity in the UN. Seventy-seven nations founded the organization, but by November 2013 the organization had since expanded to 133 member countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[137]</a></sup> The group was founded 15 June 1964 by the "Joint Declaration of the Seventy-Seven Countries" issued at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Trade_and_Development" title="United Nations Conference on Trade and Development">United Nations Conference on Trade and Development</a> (UNCTAD). The group held its first major meeting in <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> in 1967, where it adopted the Charter of Algiers and established the basis for permanent institutional structures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[138]</a></sup> With the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/New_International_Economic_Order" title="New International Economic Order">New International Economic Order</a> by developing countries in the 1970s, the work of the G77 spread throughout the UN system. Similar groupings of developing states also operate in other UN agencies, such as the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_24" title="Group of 24">Group of 24</a> (<a href="/wiki/Group_of_24" title="Group of 24">G-24</a>), which operates in the IMF on monetary affairs.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Objectives">Objectives</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peacekeeping_and_security">Peacekeeping and security</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">United Nations peacekeeping</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Nations_peacekeeping_missions" title="List of United Nations peacekeeping missions">List of United Nations peacekeeping missions</a></div>
<p>The UN, after approval by the Security Council, sends peacekeepers to regions where armed conflict has recently ceased or paused to enforce the terms of peace agreements and to discourage combatants from resuming hostilities. Since the UN does not maintain its own military, peacekeeping forces are voluntarily provided by member states. These soldiers are sometimes nicknamed "Blue Helmets" for their distinctive gear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo200452_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo200452-142">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoulon1998ix_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoulon1998ix-143">[140]</a></sup> Peacekeeping forces as a whole received the Nobel Peace Prize in 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[141]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff,_Haiti,_Feb._20,_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1848" data-file-width="2587" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg/220px-A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg/330px-A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg/440px-A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff%2C_Haiti%2C_Feb._20%2C_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_United_Nations_Peacekeeper_from_Nepal_provides_security_at_a_rice_distribution_site_in_Kenscoff,_Haiti,_Feb._20,_2010_100220-N-HX866-010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Nepalese soldier on a peacekeeping deployment providing security at a rice distribution site in Haiti during 2010</div></div></div>
<p>The UN has carried out 71 peacekeeping operations since 1947; as of April 2021, over 88,000 peacekeeping personnel from 121 nations were deployed on 12 missions, mostly in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[142]</a></sup> The largest is the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_South_Sudan" title="United Nations Mission in South Sudan">United Nations Mission in South Sudan</a> (UNMISS), which has close to 19,200 uniformed personnel;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[143]</a></sup> the smallest, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Military_Observer_Group_in_India_and_Pakistan" title="United Nations Military Observer Group in India and Pakistan">United Nations Military Observer Group in India and Pakistan</a> (UNMOGIP), consists of 113 civilians and experts charged with monitoring the ceasefire in <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(state)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (state)">Jammu and Kashmir</a>. UN peacekeepers with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Truce_Supervision_Organization" title="United Nations Truce Supervision Organization">United Nations Truce Supervision Organization</a> (UNTSO) have been stationed in the Middle East since 1948, the longest-running active peacekeeping mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNPO_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNPO-147">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>A study by the RAND Corporation in 2005 found the UN to be successful in two out of three peacekeeping efforts. It compared efforts at nation-building by the UN to those of the United States, and found that seven out of eight UN cases are at peace, as compared with four out of eight U.S. cases at peace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[145]</a></sup> Also in 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Human_Security_Report_2005" title="Human Security Report 2005">Human Security Report</a> documented a decline in the number of wars, genocides, and human rights abuses since the end of the Cold War, and presented evidence, albeit circumstantial, that international activism—mostly spearheaded by the UN—has been the main cause of the decline in armed conflict in that period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[146]</a></sup> Situations in which the UN has not only acted to keep the peace but also intervened include the Korean War (1950–53) and the authorization of intervention in Iraq after the Gulf War (1990–91).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy200756_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy200756-150">[147]</a></sup> Further studies published between 2008 and 2021 determined UN peacekeeping operations to be more effective at ensuring long-lasting peace and minimizing civilian casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-151">[148]</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="inaction_on_genocide_and_human_rights"></span>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG/210px-GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG/315px-GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG/420px-GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG 2x" width="210"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GreenLine_BufferZone_Large.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Buffer_Zone_in_Cyprus" title="UN Buffer Zone in Cyprus">UN Buffer Zone in Cyprus</a> was established in 1974 following the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish invasion of Cyprus">Turkish invasion of Cyprus</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The UN has also drawn criticism for perceived failures. In many cases, member states have shown reluctance to achieve or enforce Security Council resolutions. Disagreements in the Security Council about military action and intervention are seen as having failed to prevent the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1971_Bangladesh_Genocide" title="1971 Bangladesh Genocide">Bangladesh genocide in 1971</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBall201146_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBall201146-152">[149]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge_rule_of_Cambodia" title="Khmer Rouge rule of Cambodia">Cambodian genocide</a> in the 1970s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007187_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007187-153">[150]</a></sup> and the Rwandan genocide in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007102–105_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007102–105-154">[151]</a></sup> Similarly, UN inaction is blamed for failing to either prevent the <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica_massacre" title="Srebrenica massacre">Srebrenica massacre</a> in 1995 or complete the peacekeeping operations in 1992–93 during the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">Somali Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995294–311_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995294–311-155">[152]</a></sup> UN peacekeepers have also been accused of child rape, soliciting prostitutes, and sexual abuse during various peacekeeping missions in the Democratic Republic of the Congo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[153]</a></sup> Haiti,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[154]</a></sup> Liberia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup> Sudan and what is now South Sudan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup> Burundi, and Ivory Coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[157]</a></sup> Scientists cited UN peacekeepers from Nepal as the likely source of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9313_Haiti_cholera_outbreak" title="2010–13 Haiti cholera outbreak">2010–13 Haiti cholera outbreak</a>, which killed more than 8,000 Haitians following the 2010 Haiti earthquake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to peacekeeping, the UN is also active in encouraging <a href="/wiki/Disarmament" title="Disarmament">disarmament</a>. Regulation of armaments was included in the writing of the UN Charter in 1945 and was envisioned as a way of limiting the use of human and economic resources for their creation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chapter|V_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chapter|V-106">[105]</a></sup> The advent of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> came only weeks after the signing of the charter, resulting in the first <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_resolution" title="United Nations General Assembly resolution">resolution</a> of the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Assembly" title="General Assembly">General Assembly</a> meeting calling for specific proposals for "the elimination from national armaments of atomic weapons and of all other major weapons adaptable to mass destruction".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[159]</a></sup> The UN has been involved with arms-limitation treaties, such as the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Space_Treaty" title="Outer Space Treaty">Outer Space Treaty</a> (1967), the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons">Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons</a> (1968), the <a href="/wiki/Seabed_Arms_Control_Treaty" title="Seabed Arms Control Treaty">Seabed Arms Control Treaty</a> (1971), the <a href="/wiki/Biological_Weapons_Convention" title="Biological Weapons Convention">Biological Weapons Convention</a> (1972), the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Weapons_Convention" title="Chemical Weapons Convention">Chemical Weapons Convention</a> (1992), and the <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Treaty" title="Ottawa Treaty">Ottawa Treaty</a> (1997), which prohibits landmines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004188–189_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004188–189-163">[160]</a></sup> Three UN bodies oversee arms proliferation issues: the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_the_Prohibition_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons">Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Nuclear-Test-Ban_Treaty_Organization_Preparatory_Commission" title="Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty Organization Preparatory Commission">Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty Organization Preparatory Commission</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004189–190_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004189–190-164">[161]</a></sup> Additionally, many peacekeeping missions focus on disarmament: several operations in West Africa disarmed roughly 250,000 former combatants and secured tens of thousands of weapons and millions of munitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>
<p>One of the UN's primary purposes is "promoting and encouraging respect for human rights and for fundamental freedoms for all without distinction as to race, sex, language, or religion", and member states pledge to undertake "joint and separate action" to protect these rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CharterIX_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-CharterIX-128">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charter1_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Charter1-166">[163]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR_(27758131387).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4800" data-file-width="6054" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR_%2827758131387%29.jpg/220px-Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR_%2827758131387%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR_%2827758131387%29.jpg/330px-Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR_%2827758131387%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR_%2827758131387%29.jpg/440px-Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR_%2827758131387%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eleanor_Roosevelt_UDHR_(27758131387).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>, 1949</div></div></div>
<p>In 1948, the General Assembly adopted a <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>, drafted by a committee headed by American diplomat and activist <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a>, and including the French lawyer <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Cassin" title="René Cassin">René Cassin</a>. The document proclaims basic civil, political, and economic rights common to all human beings, though its effectiveness towards achieving these ends has been disputed since its drafting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007178–182_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007178–182-167">[164]</a></sup> The Declaration serves as a "common standard of achievement for all peoples and all nations" rather than a legally binding document, but it has become the basis of two binding treaties, the 1966 <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Civil_and_Political_Rights" title="International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights">International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Economic,_Social_and_Cultural_Rights" title="International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights">International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009377_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009377-168">[165]</a></sup> In practice, the UN is unable to take significant action against human rights abuses without a Security Council resolution, though it does substantial work in investigating and reporting abuses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007185,_188_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007185,_188-169">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1979, the General Assembly adopted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Discrimination_against_Women" title="Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women">Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Convention on the Rights of the Child">Convention on the Rights of the Child</a> in 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand200970,_73_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand200970,_73-170">[167]</a></sup> With the end of the Cold War, the push for human rights action took on new impetus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007192_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007192-171">[168]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="United Nations Commission on Human Rights">United Nations Commission on Human Rights</a> was formed in 1993 to oversee human rights issues for the UN, following the recommendation of that year's <a href="/wiki/World_Conference_on_Human_Rights" title="World Conference on Human Rights">World Conference on Human Rights</a>. Jacques Fomerand, a scholar of the UN, describes this organization's mandate as "broad and vague", with only "meagre" resources to carry it out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009347_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009347-172">[169]</a></sup> In 2006, it was replaced by a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">Human Rights Council</a> consisting of 47 nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[170]</a></sup> Also in 2006, the General Assembly passed a <a href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Rights_of_Indigenous_Peoples" title="Declaration on the Rights of Indigenous Peoples">Declaration on the Rights of Indigenous Peoples</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup> and in 2011 it passed its first resolution recognizing the rights of <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other UN bodies responsible for <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's rights</a> issues include <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_the_Status_of_Women" title="United Nations Commission on the Status of Women">United Nations Commission on the Status of Women</a>, a commission of ECOSOC founded in 1946; the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Fund_for_Women" title="United Nations Development Fund for Women">United Nations Development Fund for Women</a>, created in 1976; and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_International_Research_and_Training_Institute_for_the_Advancement_of_Women" title="United Nations International Research and Training Institute for the Advancement of Women">United Nations International Research and Training Institute for the Advancement of Women</a>, founded in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand200957,_194,_341_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand200957,_194,_341-176">[173]</a></sup> The UN Permanent Forum on Indigenous Issues, one of three bodies with a mandate to oversee issues related to indigenous peoples, held its first session in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_development_and_humanitarian_assistance">Economic development and humanitarian assistance</span></h3>
<table style="background:#f3f9ff; padding-left:7px; padding-bottom:7px; float:right; border:1px dashed #aaa; margin-left:1em; margin-bottom:1em;">
<tbody><tr>
<td colspan="2">
<p><b>Millennium Development Goals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[175]</a></sup></b>
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:top; font-size:100%;">
<ol><li>Eradicate extreme poverty and hunger</li>
<li>Achieve universal primary education</li>
<li>Promote gender equality and empower women</li>
<li>Reduce child mortality</li>
<li>Improve maternal health</li>
<li>Combat HIV/AIDS, malaria, and other diseases</li>
<li>Ensure environmental sustainability</li>
<li>Develop a global partnership for development</li></ol>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Another primary purpose of the UN is "to achieve international cooperation in solving international problems of an economic, social, cultural, or humanitarian character".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charter1_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-Charter1-166">[163]</a></sup> Numerous bodies have been created to work towards this goal, primarily under the authority of the General Assembly and ECOSOC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007143–144_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007143–144-179">[176]</a></sup> In 2000, the 192 UN member states agreed to achieve eight <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a> by 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[177]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> were launched in 2015 to succeed the Millennium Development Goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sustainable_Development_Goals_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Development_Goals-82">[81]</a></sup> The SDGs have an associated financing framework called the <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa_Action_Agenda" title="Addis Ababa Action Agenda">Addis Ababa Action Agenda</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UN Development Programme</a> (UNDP), an organization for grant-based technical assistance founded in 1945, is one of the leading bodies in the field of <a href="/wiki/International_development" title="International development">international development</a>. The organization also publishes the UN <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, a comparative measure <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">ranking countries</a> by poverty, literacy, education, life expectancy, and other factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004169–170,_172_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004169–170,_172-181">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009341–342_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009341–342-182">[179]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO), also founded in 1945, promotes agricultural development and food security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009126_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009126-183">[180]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> (the United Nations Children's Fund) was created in 1946 to aid European children after the Second World War and expanded its mission to provide aid around the world and to uphold the convention on the Rights of the Child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[182]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2220" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg/200px-Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg/300px-Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg/400px-Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Three former directors of the <a href="/wiki/Smallpox#Eradication" title="Smallpox">Global Smallpox Eradication Programme</a> reading the news that smallpox has been globally eradicated in 1980</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) are independent, specialized agencies and observers within the UN framework, according to a 1947 agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[183]</a></sup> They were initially formed separately from the UN through the <a href="/wiki/Bretton_Woods_system" title="Bretton Woods system">Bretton Woods Agreement</a> in 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[184]</a></sup> The World Bank provides loans for international development, while the IMF promotes international economic co-operation and gives emergency loans to indebted countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009175,_191–192_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009175,_191–192-188">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg/200px-Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg/300px-Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg/400px-Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iman_Mutlaq_visits_Zaatari_Refugee_Camp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, UNHCR remains responsible for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian_refugees" title="Syrian refugees">Syrian refugees</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zaatari_refugee_camp" title="Zaatari refugee camp">Zaatari refugee camp</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO), which focuses on international health issues and disease eradication, is another of the UN's largest agencies. In 1980, the agency announced that the eradication of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> had been completed. In subsequent decades, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WHO" title="WHO">WHO</a> largely eradicated <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_blindness" title="River blindness">river blindness</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leprosy" title="Leprosy">leprosy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004176–177_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004176–177-189">[186]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Joint_United_Nations_Programme_on_HIV/AIDS" title="Joint United Nations Programme on HIV/AIDS">Joint United Nations Programme on HIV/AIDS</a> (UNAIDS), begun in 1996, co-ordinates the organization's response to the AIDS epidemic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009199–200_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009199–200-190">[187]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Population_Fund" title="UN Population Fund">UN Population Fund</a>, which also dedicates part of its resources to combating HIV, is the world's largest source of funding for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reproductive_health" title="Reproductive health">reproductive health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009368_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009368-191">[188]</a></sup>
</p><p>Along with the <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement</a>, the UN often takes a leading role in co-ordinating emergency relief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004183_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004183-192">[189]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> (WFP), created in 1961, provides food aid in response to famine, natural disasters, and armed conflict. The organization reports that it feeds an average of 90 million people in 80 nations each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004183_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004183-192">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[190]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Office_of_the_United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> (UNHCR), established in 1950, works to protect the rights of refugees, asylum seekers, and stateless people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[191]</a></sup> UNHCR and WFP programmes are funded by voluntary contributions from governments, corporations, and individuals, though the UNHCR's administrative costs are paid for by the UN's primary budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009348,_398_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009348,_398-195">[192]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_and_climate">Environment and climate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a></div>
<p>Beginning with the formation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Environmental_Programme" title="UN Environmental Programme">UN Environmental Programme</a> (UNEP) in 1972, the UN has made environmental issues a prominent part of its agenda. A lack of success in the first two decades of UN work in this area led to the 1992 <a href="/wiki/Earth_Summit" title="Earth Summit">Earth Summit</a> in Rio de Janeiro, Brazil, which sought to give new impetus to these efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007160–162_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007160–162-196">[193]</a></sup> In 1988, the UNEP and the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> (WMO), another UN organization, established the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a>, which assesses and reports on research on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[194]</a></sup> The UN-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a>, signed in 1997, set legally binding emissions reduction targets for ratifying states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004179_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004179-198">[195]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_global_issues">Other global issues</span></h3>
<p>Since the UN's creation, over 80 colonies have attained independence. The General Assembly adopted the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Granting_of_Independence_to_Colonial_Countries_and_Peoples" title="Declaration on the Granting of Independence to Colonial Countries and Peoples">Declaration on the Granting of Independence to Colonial Countries and Peoples</a> in 1960 with no votes against but abstentions from all major colonial powers. The UN works towards decolonization through groups including the <a href="/wiki/Special_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="Special Committee on Decolonization">UN Committee on Decolonization</a>, created in 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[196]</a></sup> The committee lists seventeen remaining "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-self-governing_territories" title="Non-self-governing territories">non-self-governing territories</a>", the largest and most populous of which is <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[197]</a></sup>
</p><p>The UN also declares and co-ordinates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_observance" title="International observance">international observances</a> that bring awareness to issues of international interest or concern; examples include <a href="/wiki/World_Tuberculosis_Day" title="World Tuberculosis Day">World Tuberculosis Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earth_Day" title="Earth Day">Earth Day</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Year_of_Deserts_and_Desertification" title="International Year of Deserts and Desertification">International Year of Deserts and Desertification</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[198]</a></sup>
</p>

</td></tr>
