<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/21px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/32px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/41px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png 2x" width="21"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a></b>
</th>
<td><div style="height: 1.25em; width: 9.75em;"><div style="position: absolute; background-color: rgb(206, 223, 242); width:0.3em; height: 1.25em; margin: 0 0 0 0; z-index: 0;"></div><span style="position: absolute; height:1.25em; width: 9.75em; padding: 0 0 0 2em; z-index: 10;"><span class="nowrap">0.754</span></span></div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><b>Other member states</b>
</th>
<td><div style="height: 1.25em; width: 9.75em;"><div style="position: absolute; background-color: rgb(206, 223, 242); width:5.4em; height: 1.25em; margin: 0 0 0 0; z-index: 0;"></div><span style="position: absolute; height:1.25em; width: 9.75em; padding: 0 0 0 2em; z-index: 10;"><span class="nowrap">12.168</span></span></div>
</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>The UN budget for 2020 was $3.1 billion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[200]</a></sup> not including additional resources donated by members, such as peacekeeping forces.
</p><p>The UN is financed from assessed and voluntary contributions from member states. The General Assembly approves the regular budget and determines the assessment for each member. This is broadly based on the relative capacity of each country to pay, as measured by its <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">gross national income</a> (GNI), with adjustments for external debt and low per capita income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifth-2006_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-fifth-2006-204">[201]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Assembly has established the principle that the UN should not be unduly dependent on any one member to finance its operations. Thus, there is a "ceiling" rate, setting the maximum amount that any member can be assessed for the regular budget. In December 2000, the Assembly revised the scale of assessments in response to pressure from the United States. As part of that revision, the regular budget ceiling was reduced from 25% to 22%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004117_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004117-205">[202]</a></sup> For the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" title="Least developed country">least developed countries</a> (LDCs), a ceiling rate of 0.01% is applied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifth-2006_204-1"><a href="#cite_note-fifth-2006-204">[201]</a></sup> In addition to the ceiling rates, the minimum amount assessed to any member nation (or "floor" rate) is set at 0.001% of the UN budget ($55,120 for the two year budget 2013–2014).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeissDaws2009682_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeissDaws2009682-206">[203]</a></sup>
</p><p>A large share of the UN's expenditure addresses its core mission of peace and security, and this budget is assessed separately from the main organizational budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004115_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFasulo2004115-207">[204]</a></sup> The peacekeeping budget for the 2015–16 fiscal year was $8.27 billion, supporting 82,318 troops deployed in 15 missions around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNPO_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNPO-147">[144]</a></sup> UN peace operations are funded by assessments, using a formula derived from the regular funding scale that includes a weighted surcharge for the five permanent Security Council members, who must approve all peacekeeping operations. This surcharge serves to offset discounted peacekeeping assessment rates for less developed countries. The largest contributors for the <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">UN peacekeeping</a> financial operations for the period 2019–2021 are : the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (27.89%), <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (15.21%), <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (8.56%), <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (6.09%), the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (5.78%), <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (5.61%), <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (3.30%), and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (3.04%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[205]</a></sup>
</p><p>Special UN programmes not included in the regular budget, such as <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> and the World Food Programme, are financed by voluntary contributions from member governments, corporations, and private individuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[207]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Evaluations.2C_awards.2C_and_criticism"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Evaluations,_awards,_and_criticism">Evaluations, awards, and criticism</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations" title="Reform of the United Nations">Reform of the United Nations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Reform of the United Nations Security Council">Reform of the United Nations Security Council</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_United_Nations" title="Criticism of the United Nations">Criticism of the United Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2319" data-file-width="3078" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg/220px-Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg/330px-Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg/440px-Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Friedensnobelpreis_2001_Vereinte_Nationen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2001_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2001 Nobel Peace Prize">2001 Nobel Peace Prize</a> to the UN—diploma in the lobby of the <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">UN Headquarters</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evaluations">Evaluations</span></h3>
<p>In evaluating the UN as a whole, Jacques Fomerand writes that the "accomplishments of the United Nations in the last 60 years are impressive in their own terms. Progress in human development during the 20th century has been dramatic, and the UN and its agencies have certainly helped the world become a more hospitable and livable place for millions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009cviii_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009cviii-211">[208]</a></sup> Evaluating the first 50 years of the UN's history, the author Stanley Meisler writes that "the United Nations never fulfilled the hopes of its founders, but it accomplished a great deal nevertheless", citing its role in decolonization and its many successful peacekeeping efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995339_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler1995339-212">[209]</a></sup>
</p><p>British historian <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kennedy" title="Paul Kennedy">Paul Kennedy</a> states that while the organization has suffered some major setbacks, "when all its aspects are considered, the UN has brought great benefits to our generation and ... will bring benefits to our children's and grandchildren's generations as well."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007290_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007290-213">[210]</a></sup>
</p><p>Former French President <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="François Hollande">François Hollande</a> stated in 2012 that "France trusts the United Nations. She knows that no state, no matter how powerful, can solve urgent problems, fight for development and bring an end to all crises ... France wants the UN to be the centre of global governance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[211]</a></sup> In his 1953 address to the United States Committee for United Nations Day, U.S. President Dwight D. Eisenhower expressed the view that, for all its flaws, "the United Nations represents man's best organized hope to substitute the conference table for the battlefield".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[212]</a></sup>
</p><p>UN peacekeeping missions are assessed to be generally successful. An analysis of 47 peace operations by <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Page_Fortna" title="Virginia Page Fortna">Virginia Page Fortna</a> of <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> found that UN-led conflict resolution usually resulted in long-term peace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[213]</a></sup> Political scientists Hanne Fjelde, Lisa Hultman and Desiree Nilsson of <a href="/wiki/Uppsala_University" title="Uppsala University">Uppsala University</a> studied twenty years of data on peacekeeping missions, including in Lebanon, the Democratic Republic of the Congo, and the Central African Republic, concluding that they were more effective at reducing civilian casualties than counterterrorism operations by nation states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[214]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a> professor Lise Howard postulates that UN peacekeeping operations are more effective due to their emphasis on "verbal persuasion, financial inducements and coercion short of offensive military force, including surveillance and arrest", which are likelier to change the behavior of warring parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-151">[148]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h3>
<p>A number of agencies and individuals associated with the UN have won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> in recognition of their work. Two secretaries-general, Dag Hammarskjöld and Kofi Annan, were each awarded the prize (in 1961 and 2001, respectively), as were Ralph Bunche (1950), a UN negotiator, René Cassin (1968), a contributor to the Universal Declaration of Human Rights, and the US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Cordell_Hull" title="Cordell Hull">Cordell Hull</a> (1945), the latter for his role in the organization's founding. <a href="/wiki/Lester_B._Pearson" title="Lester B. Pearson">Lester B. Pearson</a>, the Canadian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_External_Affairs" title="Secretary of State for External Affairs">Secretary of State for External Affairs</a>, was awarded the prize in 1957 for his role in organizing the UN's first peacekeeping force to resolve the Suez Crisis. UNICEF won the prize in 1965, the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> in 1969, the UN Peacekeeping Forces in 1988, the International Atomic Energy Agency (which reports to the UN) in 2005, and the UN-supported <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_the_Prohibition_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons">Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons</a> in 2013. The UN High Commissioner for Refugees was awarded in 1954 and 1981, becoming one of only two recipients to win the prize twice. The UN as a whole was awarded the prize in 2001, sharing it with Annan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[215]</a></sup> In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">IPCC</a> received the prize "for their efforts to build up and disseminate greater knowledge about man-made climate change, and to lay the foundations for the measures that are needed to counteract such change."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[216]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Role">Role</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UN70.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/UN70.JPG/220px-UN70.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/UN70.JPG/330px-UN70.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/UN70.JPG/440px-UN70.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UN70.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marking of the UN's 70th anniversary – Budapest, 2015</div></div></div>
<p>In a sometimes-misquoted statement, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> stated in February 2003—referring to UN uncertainty towards Iraqi provocations under the Saddam Hussein regime—that "free nations will not allow the UN to fade into history as an ineffective, irrelevant debating society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[219]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, in his memoir <i><a href="/wiki/A_Promised_Land" title="A Promised Land">A Promised Land</a></i> noted, "In the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the chances of reaching any consensus had been slim, which is why the U.N. had stood idle as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet" title="Soviet">Soviet</a> tanks rolled into Hungary or U.S. planes dropped napalm on the Vietnamese countryside. Even after the Cold War, divisions within the Security Council continued to hamstring the U.N.'s ability to tackle problems. Its member states lacked either the means or the collective will to reconstruct failing states like Somalia, or prevent ethnic slaughter in places like Sri Lanka."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[221]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since its founding, there have been many calls for <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations" title="Reform of the United Nations">reform of the UN</a> but little consensus on how to do so. Some want the UN to play a greater or more effective role in world affairs, while others want its role reduced to humanitarian work.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Representation_and_structure">Representation and structure</span></h4>
<p>Core features of the UN apparatus, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">veto</a> privileges of some nations in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Security_Council" title="Security Council">Security Council</a>, are often described as fundamentally undemocratic, contrary to the UN mission, and a main cause of inaction on genocides and crimes against humanity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[223]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jacques Fomerand states the most enduring divide in views of the UN is "the North–South split" between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_divide_in_the_World" title="North–South divide in the World">richer Northern nations and developing Southern nations</a>. Southern nations tend to favour a more empowered UN with a stronger General Assembly, allowing them a greater voice in world affairs, while Northern nations prefer an economically <a href="/wiki/Laissez-faire" title="Laissez-faire">laissez-faire</a> UN that focuses on transnational threats such as terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009civ_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFomerand2009civ-227">[224]</a></sup>
</p><p>There have also been numerous calls for the <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Reform of the United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council's membership to be increased</a>, for different ways of electing the UN's secretary-general, and for a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="United Nations Parliamentary Assembly">UN Parliamentary Assembly</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Exclusion_of_countries">Exclusion of countries</span></h4>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/French_Committee_of_National_Liberation" title="French Committee of National Liberation">French Committee of National Liberation</a> was late to be recognized by the U.S. as the government of France, and so the country was initially excluded from the conferences that created the new organization. Future French president <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> criticized the UN, famously calling it a <i>machin</i> ("contraption"), and was not convinced that a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_security" title="Global security">global security</a> alliance would help maintain world peace, preferring <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_France" title="Foreign relations of France">direct defence treaties</a> between countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[225]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1971, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (ROC), or Taiwan, has <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_1668" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 1668">been excluded from the UN</a> and consistently denied membership in its reapplications; Taiwanese citizens are also barred from entering UN facilities with <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_passport" title="Taiwan passport">ROC passports</a>. The UN officially adheres to the "<a href="/wiki/One_China" title="One China">One China</a>" policy endorsed by most member states, which recognizes the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC), a permanent member of the UN Security Council, as the only legitimate Chinese government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[226]</a></sup> Critics allege that this position reflects a failure of the organization's development goals and guidelines,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[227]</a></sup> and it garnered renewed scrutiny during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, when Taiwan was denied membership in the World Health Organization despite its <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Taiwan" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Taiwan">relatively effective response to the virus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[228]</a></sup> Support for Taiwan's inclusion is subject to pressure from the PRC, which regards the territories administered by the ROC <a href="/wiki/One_China" title="One China">as their own territory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[230]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h4>
<p>Throughout the Cold War, both the US and USSR repeatedly accused the UN of favouring the other. In 1950, the USSR boycotted the organization in protest to <a href="/wiki/China_and_the_United_Nations" title="China and the United Nations">China's seat at the UN Security Council</a> being given to the anticommunist government of the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a>. Three years later, the Soviets effectively forced the resignation of UN Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Trygve_Lie" title="Trygve Lie">Trygve Lie</a> by refusing to acknowledge his administration due to his support of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[231]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ironically, the US had simultaneously scrutinized the UN for employing communists and Soviet sympathizers, following a high-profile accusation that <a href="/wiki/Alger_Hiss" title="Alger Hiss">Alger Hiss</a>, an American who had taken part in the establishment of the UN, had been a Soviet spy. US Senator Joseph McCarthy claimed that the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">UN Secretariat</a> under Secretary-General Lie harbored American communists, leading to further pressure that the UN chief resign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[232]</a></sup> The US saw nascent opposition to the UN into the 1960s, particularly among political conservatives, with groups such as the <a href="/wiki/John_Birch_Society" title="John Birch Society">John Birch Society</a> alleging that the organization was an instrument for communism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[233]</a></sup> Popular opposition to the UN was expressed through bumper stickers and signs with slogans such as "Get the U.S. out of the U.N. and the U.N. out of the U.S.!" and "You can't spell communism without U.N."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeisler199572–73,_82_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeisler199572–73,_82-237">[234]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bias">Bias</span></h4>
<p>The UN's attention to Israel's treatment of Palestinians is considered excessive by a range of critics, including Israeli diplomat <a href="/wiki/Dore_Gold" title="Dore Gold">Dore Gold</a>, British scholar <a href="/wiki/Robert_S._Wistrich" title="Robert S. Wistrich">Robert S. Wistrich</a>, American legal scholar <a href="/wiki/Alan_Dershowitz" title="Alan Dershowitz">Alan Dershowitz</a>, Australian politician <a href="/wiki/Mark_Dreyfus" title="Mark Dreyfus">Mark Dreyfus</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[235]</a></sup> In September 2015, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>'s Faisal bin Hassan Trad was elected chair of an advisory committee in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">UN Human Rights Council</a> that appoints independent experts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[236]</a></sup> a move criticized by human rights groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[238]</a></sup> The UNHRC has likewise been accused of anti-Israel bias, as it has passed more resolutions condemning Israel than the rest of the world combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[239]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effectiveness">Effectiveness</span></h4>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> scholar <a href="/wiki/Edward_Luck" title="Edward Luck">Edward Luck</a>, former director of the Center on International Organization of the <a href="/wiki/School_of_International_and_Public_Affairs,_Columbia_University" title="School of International and Public Affairs, Columbia University">School of International and Public Affairs of Columbia University</a>, the United States has preferred a feeble United Nations in major projects undertaken by the organization so as to forestall UN interference with, or resistance to, American policies. "The last thing the U.S. wants is an independent U.N. throwing its weight around," Luck said. Similarly, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Ambassador_to_the_United_Nations" title="US Ambassador to the United Nations">US Ambassador to the United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Patrick_Moynihan" title="Daniel Patrick Moynihan">Daniel Patrick Moynihan</a> explained that "The Department of State desired that the United Nations prove utterly ineffective in whatever measures it undertook. The task was given to me, and I carried it forward with not inconsiderable success."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[240]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, former special representative of the secretary-general of the UN to <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Sahnoun" title="Mohamed Sahnoun">Mohamed Sahnoun</a> published <i>Somalia: The Missed Opportunities</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[241]</a></sup> a book in which he analyses the reasons for the failure of the 1992 UN intervention in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>. Sahnoun claims that between the start of the Somali civil war in 1988 and the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Siad_Barre" title="Siad Barre">Siad Barre</a> regime in January 1991, the UN missed at least three opportunities to prevent major human tragedies; when the UN tried to provide humanitarian assistance, they were totally outperformed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NGO" title="NGO">NGOs</a>, whose competence and dedication sharply contrasted with the UN's excessive caution and bureaucratic inefficiencies. Sahnoun warned that if radical reform were not undertaken, then the UN would continue to respond to such crises with inept improvisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>Beyond specific instances or areas of alleged ineffectiveness, some scholars debate about the overall effectiveness of the UN. Adherents to the <a href="/wiki/Realism_(international_relations)" title="Realism (international relations)">realist</a> school of thought take a pessimistic position, arguing that the UN is not an effective organization because it is dominated and constrained by great powers. <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_(international_relations)" title="Liberalism (international relations)">Liberal</a> scholars counter that it is an effective organization because it has proved capable of solving many problems by working around the restrictions imposed by powerful member states; the UN is generally considered by scholars to be more effective in realms such as public health, humanitarian assistance, and conflict resolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[243]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inefficiency_and_corruption">Inefficiency and corruption</span></h4>
<p>Critics have also accused the UN of bureaucratic inefficiency, waste, and corruption. In 1976, the General Assembly established the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Inspection_Unit" title="Joint Inspection Unit">Joint Inspection Unit</a> to seek out inefficiencies within the UN system. During the 1990s, the US withheld dues citing inefficiency and only started repayment on the condition that a major reforms initiative be introduced. In 1994, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_of_Internal_Oversight_Services" title="United Nations Office of Internal Oversight Services">Office of Internal Oversight Services</a> (OIOS) was established by the General Assembly to serve as an efficiency watchdog.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[244]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, the UN faced accusations that its recently ended <a href="/wiki/Oil-for-Food_Programme" title="Oil-for-Food Programme">Oil-for-Food Programme</a> — in which Iraq had been allowed to trade oil for basic needs to relieve the pressure of sanctions — had suffered from widespread corruption, including billions of dollars of <a href="/wiki/Kickback_(bribery)" title="Kickback (bribery)">kickbacks</a>. An independent inquiry created by the UN found that many of its officials had been involved in <a href="/wiki/Oil-for-Food_Program_Hearings" title="Oil-for-Food Program Hearings">the scheme</a>, and raised "significant" questions about the role of <a href="/wiki/Kojo_Annan" title="Kojo Annan">Kojo Annan</a>, the son of Kofi Annan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[245]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Model_United_Nations">Model United Nations</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a></div>
<p>The United Nations has inspired the extracurricular activity <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a> (MUN). MUN is a simulation of United Nations activity based on the UN agenda and following UN procedure. It is usually attended by high school and university students who organize conferences to simulate the various UN committees to discuss important issues of the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[246]</a></sup> Today, MUN educates tens of thousands on the activities of the UN around the world. MUN has many famous and notable alumni, such as former UN Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[247]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Poland had not been represented among the fifty nations at the San Francisco conference due to the reluctance of the Western superpowers to recognize its post-war communist government. However, the Charter was later amended to list Poland as a founding member, and Poland ratified the Charter on 16 October 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrant200925–26_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrant200925–26-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some sources identify seventeen specialized agencies, taking into account the three specialized agencies that make up the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a>, which is now treated as one organization: the <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">International Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a> (IBRD), the <a href="/wiki/International_Development_Association" title="International Development Association">International Development Association</a> (IDA), and the <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Corporation" title="International Finance Corporation">International Finance Corporation</a> (IFC).</span>
</li>

</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Citations">Citations</span></h3>

<li id="cite_note-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-104">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.un.org/en/ga/about/ropga/plenary.shtml" rel="nofollow">"General Assembly of the United Nations: Rules of Procedure: XII – Plenary Meetings"</a>. United Nations. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120113095649/http://www.un.org/en/ga/about/ropga/plenary.shtml" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 13 January 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">4 December</span> 2013</span>. <q>Decisions of the General Assembly on important questions shall be made by a two-thirds majority of the members present and voting. These questions shall include: recommendations with respect to the maintenance of international peace and security, the election of the non-permanent members of the Security Council, the election of the members of the Economic and Social Council, the election of members of the Trusteeship Council in accordance with paragraph 1 c of Article 86 of the Charter, the admission of new Members to the United Nations, the suspension of the rights and privileges of membership, the expulsion of Members, questions relating to the operation of the trusteeship system, and budgetary questions.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=General+Assembly+of+the+United+Nations%3A+Rules+of+Procedure%3A+XII+%E2%80%93+Plenary+Meetings&amp;rft.pub=United+Nations&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.un.org%2Fen%2Fga%2Fabout%2Fropga%2Fplenary.shtml&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUnited+Nations"></span></span>
